# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
#saca2 ^4kQG4nJZ

ADD ^8mfiGoBe

P
C ^3BsvWf0w

MEMORY ^3QY4dUqO

Reg file ^1lOJ6cKt

ALU ^WfspwXy1

Immediate
generator ^I0dice4L

regwrite ^p2ksl8JS

MEMORY ^GwaRd7CH

memread ^VtbsFXH8

memwrite ^AtYDzk02

branch ^SulvYQtR

memtoreg ^ckoR4h0H

ALU control ^BdJN3Kgs

ALUop ^9SOoJvx4

ALUop ^R5NYAYbu

00 add
01 R-format
10 subtract ^3nY49oZ7

ALUsrc ^5hvQPPLb

z ^alLzbQ41

z=1 if ALU operation gives 0, otherwise z=0 (useful for branches ⟶ beq x, y = is x-y=0) ^qTnoM10S

control ^7Bb3lcoO

branch ^3Rdl5pvF

ALUop ^zw8Va1Ec

Don't care ⟶ control bit could be either 0 or 1 at a certain instance, doesn't affect result. The designer sets the don't care, we do not say ^F5QogXSK

used in operations that need to subtract (compare numbers) (beq, bneq, etc) ^VbpMUvJ9

used in operations that need to add, aggregate an offset(sw, lw, etc) ^S8TOmFP2

used in R-format operations (add, sub, and, or, etc) ^xlw0TOxe

REMARK: sub ^ and, don't use 10 ^ 00 respectively as ALUop depends on opcode. And they have = opcode ∴ we could not have 10 on sub and 00 on add (we would always get 00 or 10) ^yezI1H8o

Garbage ⟶ intermediate bit/s of the architecture, that at a certain instruction, do not have any meaning and are not used (they exist but are useless and meaningless) ^UdkyBhre

Exercise: evaluate each internal bits value (in decimal) for some instructions (beq, add, addi, sw, lw, etc) and the value of the control bits to run that instruction.  ^p4wFpQZH
